# big-code-pg-arch-001: PostgreSQL Query Execution Pipeline

## Task

Trace the PostgreSQL query execution pipeline from parse to execute. Starting from `exec_simple_query()` in the traffic cop, map how a SQL string flows through the parser (lexer + grammar), semantic analyzer, query rewriter, planner/optimizer, and executor, identifying the data structures that flow between each stage.

## Context

- **Repository**: postgres/postgres (C, ~1.5M LOC)
- **Category**: Architectural Understanding
- **Difficulty**: hard
- **Subsystem Focus**: src/backend/ — parser, rewrite, optimizer, executor subsystems

## Requirements

1. Identify all files involved in the query pipeline (traffic cop, parser, analyzer, rewriter, planner, executor, node type definitions)
2. Trace the dependency chain from `exec_simple_query()` through each pipeline stage, identifying the data type transformations (RawStmt -> Query -> PlannedStmt -> tuples)
3. Document the two-phase optimization (Path generation via allpaths.c, then Plan creation via createplan.c)
4. Explain the Volcano-style executor dispatch in execProcnode.c

## Expected Output

Write your analysis to `/logs/agent/solution.md` with the following structure:

```
## Files Examined
- path/to/file1.ext — role in architecture
- path/to/file2.ext — role in architecture
...

## Dependency Chain
1. Entry point: path/to/entry.ext
2. Calls: path/to/next.ext (via function/method name)
3. Delegates to: path/to/impl.ext
...

## Analysis
[Detailed architectural analysis including:
- Design patterns identified
- Component responsibilities
- Data flow description
- Interface contracts between components]

## Summary
[Concise 2-3 sentence summary answering the task question]
```

## Evaluation Criteria

- File recall: Did you find the correct set of architecturally relevant files?
- Dependency accuracy: Did you trace the correct dependency/call chain?
- Architectural coherence: Did you correctly identify the design patterns and component relationships?

   603→pg_parse_query(const char *query_string)
   604→{
   605→	List	   *raw_parsetree_list;
   606→
   607→	TRACE_POSTGRESQL_QUERY_PARSE_START(query_string);
   608→
   609→	if (log_parser_stats)
   610→		ResetUsage();
   611→
   612→	raw_parsetree_list = raw_parser(query_string, RAW_PARSE_DEFAULT);
   613→
   614→	if (log_parser_stats)
   615→		ShowUsage("PARSER STATISTICS");
   616→
   617→#ifdef DEBUG_NODE_TESTS_ENABLED
   618→
   619→	/* Optional debugging check: pass raw parsetrees through copyObject() */
   620→	if (Debug_copy_parse_plan_trees)
   621→	{
   622→		List	   *new_list = copyObject(raw_parsetree_list);
   623→
   624→		/* This checks both copyObject() and the equal() routines... */
   625→		if (!equal(new_list, raw_parsetree_list))
   626→			elog(WARNING, "copyObject() failed to produce an equal raw parse tree");
   627→		else
   628→			raw_parsetree_list = new_list;
   629→	}
   630→
   631→	/*
   632→	 * Optional debugging check: pass raw parsetrees through
   633→	 * outfuncs/readfuncs
   634→	 */
   635→	if (Debug_write_read_parse_plan_trees)
   636→	{
   637→		char	   *str = nodeToStringWithLocations(raw_parsetree_list);
   638→		List	   *new_list = stringToNodeWithLocations(str);
   639→
   640→		pfree(str);
   641→		/* This checks both outfuncs/readfuncs and the equal() routines... */
   642→		if (!equal(new_list, raw_parsetree_list))
   643→			elog(WARNING, "outfuncs/readfuncs failed to produce an equal raw parse tree");
   644→		else
   645→			raw_parsetree_list = new_list;
   646→	}
   647→
   648→#endif							/* DEBUG_NODE_TESTS_ENABLED */
   649→
   650→	TRACE_POSTGRESQL_QUERY_PARSE_DONE(query_string);
   651→
   652→	return raw_parsetree_list;
   653→}

   674→	TRACE_POSTGRESQL_QUERY_REWRITE_START(query_string);

   677→	 * (1) Perform parse analysis.
   678→	 */

   970→pg_plan_queries(List *querytrees, const char *query_string, int cursorOptions,
   971→				ParamListInfo boundParams)
   972→{
   973→	List	   *stmt_list = NIL;
   974→	ListCell   *query_list;
   975→
   976→	foreach(query_list, querytrees)
   977→	{
   978→		Query	   *query = lfirst_node(Query, query_list);
   979→		PlannedStmt *stmt;
   980→
   981→		if (query->commandType == CMD_UTILITY)
   982→		{
   983→			/* Utility commands require no planning. */
   984→			stmt = makeNode(PlannedStmt);
   985→			stmt->commandType = CMD_UTILITY;
   986→			stmt->canSetTag = query->canSetTag;
   987→			stmt->utilityStmt = query->utilityStmt;
   988→			stmt->stmt_location = query->stmt_location;
   989→			stmt->stmt_len = query->stmt_len;
   990→			stmt->queryId = query->queryId;
   991→		}
   992→		else
   993→		{
   994→			stmt = pg_plan_query(query, query_string, cursorOptions,
   995→								 boundParams);
   996→		}
   997→
   998→		stmt_list = lappend(stmt_list, stmt);
   999→	}
  1000→
  1001→	return stmt_list;
  1002→}

   882→pg_plan_query(Query *querytree, const char *query_string, int cursorOptions,
   883→			  ParamListInfo boundParams)
   884→{
   885→	PlannedStmt *plan;
   886→
   887→	/* Utility commands have no plans. */
   888→	if (querytree->commandType == CMD_UTILITY)
   889→		return NULL;
   890→
   891→	/* Planner must have a snapshot in case it calls user-defined functions. */
   892→	Assert(ActiveSnapshotSet());
   893→
   894→	TRACE_POSTGRESQL_QUERY_PLAN_START();
   895→
   896→	if (log_planner_stats)
   897→		ResetUsage();
   898→
   899→	/* call the optimizer */
   900→	plan = planner(querytree, query_string, cursorOptions, boundParams);
   901→
   902→	if (log_planner_stats)
   903→		ShowUsage("PLANNER STATISTICS");
   904→
   905→#ifdef DEBUG_NODE_TESTS_ENABLED
   906→
   907→	/* Optional debugging check: pass plan tree through copyObject() */
   908→	if (Debug_copy_parse_plan_trees)
   909→	{
   910→		PlannedStmt *new_plan = copyObject(plan);
   911→
   912→		/*
   913→		 * equal() currently does not have routines to compare Plan nodes, so
   914→		 * don't try to test equality here.  Perhaps fix someday?
   915→		 */
   916→#ifdef NOT_USED
   917→		/* This checks both copyObject() and the equal() routines... */
   918→		if (!equal(new_plan, plan))
   919→			elog(WARNING, "copyObject() failed to produce an equal plan tree");
   920→		else
   921→#endif
   922→			plan = new_plan;
   923→	}
   924→
   925→	/* Optional debugging check: pass plan tree through outfuncs/readfuncs */
   926→	if (Debug_write_read_parse_plan_trees)

   928→		char	   *str;
   929→		PlannedStmt *new_plan;
   930→
   931→		str = nodeToStringWithLocations(plan);

   933→		pfree(str);

   936→		 * equal() currently do
... (truncated)

   100→
   101→/*
   102→ * Query -
   103→ *	  Parse analysis turns all statements into a Query tree
   104→ *	  for further processing by the rewriter and planner.
   105→ *
   106→ *	  Utility statements (i.e. non-optimizable statements) have the
   107→ *	  utilityStmt field set, and the rest of the Query is mostly dummy.
   108→ *
   109→ *	  Planning converts a Query tree into a Plan tree headed by a PlannedStmt
   110→ *	  node --- the Query structure is not used by the executor.
   111→ *
   112→ *	  All the fields ignored for the query jumbling are not semantically
   113→ *	  significant (such as alias names), as is ignored anything that can
   114→ *	  be deduced from child nodes (else we'd just be double-hashing that
   115→ *	  piece of information).
   116→ */
   117→typedef struct Query
   118→{
   119→	NodeTag		type;
   120→
   121→	CmdType		commandType;	/* select|insert|update|delete|merge|utility */
   122→
   123→	/* where did I come from? */
   124→	QuerySource querySource pg_node_attr(query_jumble_ignore);
   125→
   126→	/*
   127→	 * query identifier (can be set by plugins); ignored for equal, as it
   128→	 * might not be set; also not stored.  This is the result of the query
   129→	 * jumble, hence ignored.
   130→	 *
   131→	 * We store this as a signed value as this is the form it's displayed to
   132→	 * users in places such as EXPLAIN and pg_stat_statements.  Primarily this
   133→	 * is done due to lack of an SQL type to represent the full range of
   134→	 * uint64.
   135→	 */
   136→	int64		queryId pg_node_attr(equal_ignore, query_jumble_ignore, read_write_ignore, read_as(0));
   137→
   138→	/* do I set the command result tag? */
   139→	bool		canSetTag pg_node_attr(query_jumble_ignore);
   140→
   141→	Node	   *utilityStmt;	/* non-nu
... (truncated)

    31→/* ----------------

    36→ *

    40→ * (We do use canSetTag, stmt_location, stmt_len, and possibly queryId.)
    41→ *
    42→ * PlannedStmt, as well as all varieties of Plan, do not support equal(),
    43→ * not because it's not sensible but because we currently have no need.

   166→ * make_one_rel
   167→ *	  Finds all possible access paths for executing a query, returning a
   168→ *	  single rel that represents the join of all base rels in the query.
   169→ */
   170→RelOptInfo *
   171→make_one_rel(PlannerInfo *root, List *joinlist)
   172→{
   173→	RelOptInfo *rel;
   174→	Index		rti;
   175→	double		total_pages;
   176→
   177→	/* Mark base rels as to whether we care about fast-start plans */
   178→	set_base_rel_consider_startup(root);
   179→
   180→	/*
   181→	 * Compute size estimates and consider_parallel flags for each base rel.
   182→	 */
   183→	set_base_rel_sizes(root);
   184→
   185→	/*
   186→	 * We should now have size estimates for every actual table involved in
   187→	 * the query, and we also know which if any have been deleted from the
   188→	 * query by join removal, pruned by partition pruning, or eliminated by
   189→	 * constraint exclusion.  So we can now compute total_table_pages.
   190→	 *
   191→	 * Note that appendrels are not double-counted here, even though we don't
   192→	 * bother to distinguish RelOptInfos for appendrel parents, because the
   193→	 * parents will have pages = 0.
   194→	 *
   195→	 * XXX if a table is self-joined, we will count it once per appearance,
   196→	 * which perhaps is the wrong thing ... but that's not completely clear,
   197→	 * and detecting self-joins here is difficult, so ignore it for now.
   198→	 */
   199→	total_pages = 0;
   200→	for (rti = 1; rti < root->simple_rel_array_size; rti++)
   201→	{
   202→		RelOptInfo *brel = root->simple_rel_array[rti];
   203→
   204→		/* there may be empty slots corresponding to non-baserel RTEs */
   205→		if (brel == NULL)
   206→			continue;
   207→
   208→		Assert(brel->relid == rti); /* sanity check on array */
   209→
   2

   286→PlannedStmt *
   287→planner(Query *parse, const char *query_string, int cursorOptions,
   288→		ParamListInfo boundParams)
   289→{

   291→

   299→	return result;
   300→}

   337→create_plan(PlannerInfo *root, Path *best_path)
   338→{
   339→	Plan	   *plan;
   340→
   341→	/* plan_params should not be in use in current query level */
   342→	Assert(root->plan_params == NIL);
   343→
   344→	/* Initialize this module's workspace in PlannerInfo */
   345→	root->curOuterRels = NULL;
   346→	root->curOuterParams = NIL;
   347→
   348→	/* Recursively process the path tree, demanding the correct tlist result */
   349→	plan = create_plan_recurse(root, best_path, CP_EXACT_TLIST);
   350→
   351→	/*
   352→	 * Make sure the topmost plan node's targetlist exposes the original
   353→	 * column names and other decorative info.  Targetlists generated within
   354→	 * the planner don't bother with that stuff, but we must have it on the
   355→	 * top-level tlist seen at execution time.  However, ModifyTable plan
   356→	 * nodes don't have a tlist matching the querytree targetlist.
   357→	 */
   358→	if (!IsA(plan, ModifyTable))
   359→		apply_tlist_labeling(plan->targetlist, root->processed_tlist);
   360→
   361→	/*
   362→	 * Attach any initPlans created in this query level to the topmost plan
   363→	 * node.  (In principle the initplans could go in any plan node at or
   364→	 * above where they're referenced, but there seems no reason to put them
   365→	 * any lower than the topmost node for the query level.  Also, see
   366→	 * comments for SS_finalize_plan before you try to change this.)
   367→	 */
   368→	SS_attach_initplans(root, plan);
   369→
   370→	/* Check we successfully assigned all NestLoopParams to plan nodes */
   371→	if (root->curOuterParams != NIL)
   372→		elog(ERROR, "failed to assign all NestLoopParams to plan nodes");
   373→
   374→	/*
   375→	 * Reset plan_params to ensure param IDs used for nestloop params are not

   149→ * All plan nodes "derive" from the Plan structure by having the
   150→ * Plan structure as the first field.  This ensures that everything works
   151→ * when nodes are cast to Plan's.  (node pointers are frequently cast to Plan*
   152→ * when passed around generically in the executor)
   153→ *
   154→ * We never actually instantiate any Plan nodes; this is just the common
   155→ * abstract superclass for all Plan-type nodes.
   156→ * ----------------
   157→ */

   167→	/* count of disabled nodes */

   169→	/* cost expended before fetching any tuples */
   170→	Cost		startup_cost;
   171→	/* total cost (assuming all tuples fetched) */
   172→	Cost		total_cost;

   175→	 * planner's estimate of result size of this plan step

   177→	/* number of rows plan is expected to emit */

   182→	/*
   183→	 * information needed for parallel query

   186→	bool		parallel_aware;

   193→	/* engage asynchronous-capable logic? */

  1687→/*
  1688→ * ParamPathInfo
  1689→ *
  1690→ * All parameterized paths for a given relation with given required outer rels
  1691→ * link to a single ParamPathInfo, which stores common information such as
  1692→ * the estimated rowcount for this parameterization.  We do this partly to
  1693→ * avoid recalculations, but mostly to ensure that the estimated rowcount
  1694→ * is in fact the same for every such path.

  3345→ * make_rel_from_joinlist
  3346→ *	  Build access paths using a "joinlist" to guide the join path search.
  3347→ *
  3348→ * See comments for deconstruct_jointree() for definition of the joinlist
  3349→ * data structure.
  3350→ */
  3351→static RelOptInfo *
  3352→make_rel_from_joinlist(PlannerInfo *root, List *joinlist)
  3353→{
  3354→	int			levels_needed;
  3355→	List	   *initial_rels;
  3356→	ListCell   *jl;
  3357→
  3358→	/*
  3359→	 * Count the number of child joinlist nodes.  This is the depth of the
  3360→	 * dynamic-programming algorithm we must employ to consider all ways of
  3361→	 * joining the child nodes.
  3362→	 */
  3363→	levels_needed = list_length(joinlist);
  3364→
  3365→	if (levels_needed <= 0)
  3366→		return NULL;			/* nothing to do? */
  3367→
  3368→	/*
  3369→	 * Construct a list of rels corresponding to the child joinlist nodes.
  3370→	 * This may contain both base rels and rels constructed according to
  3371→	 * sub-joinlists.
  3372→	 */
  3373→	initial_rels = NIL;
  3374→	foreach(jl, joinlist)
  3375→	{
  3376→		Node	   *jlnode = (Node *) lfirst(jl);
  3377→		RelOptInfo *thisrel;
  3378→
  3379→		if (IsA(jlnode, RangeTblRef))
  3380→		{
  3381→			int			varno = ((RangeTblRef *) jlnode)->rtindex;
  3382→
  3383→			thisrel = find_base_rel(root, varno);
  3384→		}
  3385→		else if (IsA(jlnode, List))
  3386→		{
  3387→			/* Recurse to handle subproblem */
  3388→			thisrel = make_rel_from_joinlist(root, (List *) jlnode);
  3389→		}
  3390→		else
  3391→		{
  3392→			elog(ERROR, "unrecognized joinlist node type: %d",
  3393→				 (int) nodeTag(jlnode));
  3394→			thisrel = NULL;		/* keep compiler quiet */
  3395→		}
  3396→
  3397→		initial_rels = lappend(initial_rels, thisrel);
  3398→	}
  3399→
  3400→	if (levels_needed == 1)
 
... (truncated)

  3428→ * standard_join_search
  3429→ *	  Find possible joinpaths for a query by successively finding ways
  3430→ *	  to join component relations into join relations.
  3431→ *
  3432→ * 'levels_needed' is the number of iterations needed, ie, the number of
  3433→ *		independent jointree items in the query.  This is > 1.
  3434→ *
  3435→ * 'initial_rels' is a list of RelOptInfo nodes for each independent
  3436→ *		jointree item.  These are the components to be joined together.
  3437→ *		Note that levels_needed == list_length(initial_rels).
  3438→ *
  3439→ * Returns the final level of join relations, i.e., the relation that is
  3440→ * the result of joining all the original relations together.
  3441→ * At least one implementation path must be provided for this relation and
  3442→ * all required sub-relations.
  3443→ *
  3444→ * To support loadable plugins that modify planner behavior by changing the
  3445→ * join searching algorithm, we provide a hook variable that lets a plugin
  3446→ * replace or supplement this function.  Any such hook must return the same
  3447→ * final join relation as the standard code would, but it might have a
  3448→ * different set of implementation paths attached, and only the sub-joinrels
  3449→ * needed for these paths need have been instantiated.
  3450→ *
  3451→ * Note to plugin authors: the functions invoked during standard_join_search()
  3452→ * modify root->join_rel_list and root->join_rel_hash.  If you want to do more
  3453→ * than one join-order search, you'll probably need to save and restore the
  3454→ * original states of those data structures.  See geqo_eval() for an example.
  3455→ */
  3456→RelOptInfo *
  3457→standard_join_search(PlannerInfo *root, int levels_needed, List *initial_rels)

  3459→	int

   327→ * set_base_rel_pathlists
   328→ *	  Finds all paths available for scanning each base-relation entry.
   329→ *	  Sequential scan and any available indices are considered.
   330→ *	  Each useful path is attached to its relation's 'pathlist' field.
   331→ */
   332→static void
   333→set_base_rel_pathlists(PlannerInfo *root)
   334→{
   335→	Index		rti;
   336→
   337→	for (rti = 1; rti < root->simple_rel_array_size; rti++)
   338→	{
   339→		RelOptInfo *rel = root->simple_rel_array[rti];
   340→
   341→		/* there may be empty slots corresponding to non-baserel RTEs */
   342→		if (rel == NULL)
   343→			continue;
   344→
   345→		Assert(rel->relid == rti);	/* sanity check on array */
   346→
   347→		/* ignore RTEs that are "other rels" */
   348→		if (rel->reloptkind != RELOPT_BASEREL)
   349→			continue;
   350→
   351→		set_rel_pathlist(root, rel, rti, root->simple_rte_array[rti]);
   352→	}
   353→}

## PostgreSQL Planner/Optimizer Architecture Report

Based on my analysis of the PostgreSQL codebase (version 18.2), here's a comprehensive overview of the planner/optimizer architecture:

### 1. Main Entry Point: `planner()` Function

**File:** `/workspace/src/backend/optimizer/plan/planner.c:287`

```c
PlannedStmt *planner(Query *parse, const char *query_string, 
                    int cursorOptions, ParamListInfo boundParams)
```

**What it does:**
- Main external interface to the query optimizer
- Can be hooked by plugins via `planner_hook`
- Delegates to `standard_planner()` if no hook is installed
- Reports the plan ID for statistics

### 2. Two-Phase Optimization Process

The PostgreSQL planner uses a clear two-phase architecture:

#### **Phase 1: Path Generation** 
- **Location:** `src/backend/optimizer/path/allpaths.c`
- **Key Function:** `make_one_rel()` (line 171)
- **Purpose:** Generate alternative execution paths for the query

#### **Phase 2: Plan Creation**
- **Location:** `src/backend/optimizer/plan/createplan.c`
- **Key Function:** `create_plan()` (line 337)
- **Purpose:** Convert the best path into an executable plan tree

### 3. Key Functions and Call Sequence

The main planning pipeline follows this sequence in `standard_planner()`:

```
standard_planner()
  ├─ subquery_planner()
  │   └─ query_planner()
  │       ├─ setup_simple_rel_arrays()

  │       ├─ deconstruct_jointree()
  │       ├─ generate_base_implied_equalities()
  │       └─ make_one_rel()    [PHASE 1: Path Generation]
  │           ├─ set_base_rel_sizes()

  │           └─ make_rel_from

     6→ * INTERFACE ROUTINES
     7→ *	ExecutorStart()
     8→ *	ExecutorRun()
     9→ *	ExecutorFinish()
    10→ *	ExecutorEnd()
    11→ *
    12→ *	These four procedures are the external interface to the executor.
    13→ *	In each case, the query descriptor is required as an argument.
    14→ *
    15→ *	ExecutorStart must be called at the beginning of execution of any
    16→ *	query plan and ExecutorEnd must always be called at the end of
    17→ *	execution of a plan (unless it is aborted due to error).
    18→ *
    19→ *	ExecutorRun accepts direction and count arguments that specify whether

    21→ *	In some cases ExecutorRun may be called multiple times to process all
    22→ *	the tuples for a plan.  It is also acceptable to stop short of executing
    23→ *	the whole plan (but only if it is a SELECT).
    24→ *
    25→ *	ExecutorFinish must be called after the final ExecutorRun call and
    26→ *	before ExecutorEnd.  This can be omitted only in case of EXPLAIN,
    27→ *	which should also omit ExecutorRun.

    23→/*----------
    24→ * The executor stores tuples in a "tuple table" which is a List of
    25→ * independent TupleTableSlots.
    26→ *
    27→ * There's various different types of tuple table slots, each being able to
    28→ * store different types of tuples. Additional types of slots can be added
    29→ * without modifying core code. The type of a slot is determined by the
    30→ * TupleTableSlotOps* passed to the slot creation routine. The builtin types
    31→ * of slots are
    32→ *
    33→ * 1. physical tuple in a disk buffer page (TTSOpsBufferHeapTuple)
    34→ * 2. physical tuple constructed in palloc'ed memory (TTSOpsHeapTuple)
    35→ * 3. "minimal" physical tuple constructed in palloc'ed memory
    36→ *    (TTSOpsMinimalTuple)
    37→ * 4. "virtual" tuple consisting of Datum/isnull arrays (TTSOpsVirtual)
    38→ *
    39→ *
    40→ * The first two cases are similar in that they both deal with "materialized"
    41→ * tuples, but resource management is different.  For a tuple in a disk page
    42→ * we need to hold a pin on the buf

Perfect! Now I have all the information I need. Let me compile a comprehensive report on the PostgreSQL executor architecture.

## PostgreSQL Executor Architecture: The Volcano-Style Tuple Execution Model

Based on my analysis of the PostgreSQL codebase (version 18.2), here's a comprehensive explanation of how the Volcano-style tuple execution model works:

---

### 1. EXECUTOR ENTRY POINTS

#### **ExecutorStart() - Initialize Execution**
**File:** `/workspace/src/backend/executor/execMain.c` (lines 121-264)

```c
void
ExecutorStart(QueryDesc *queryDesc, int eflags)
{
    if (ExecutorStart_hook)
        (*ExecutorStart_hook) (queryDesc, eflags);
    else
        standard_ExecutorStart(queryDesc, eflags);
}
```

**What happens:**
1. Creates an `EState` (execution state) - the global context for execution
2. Sets up memory contexts for the query
3. Calls `InitPlan()` which recursively initializes the plan tree via `ExecInitNode()`
4. Creates expression contexts for evaluating predicates
5. Registers the snapshot for tuple visibility
6. Sets up AFTER triggers if needed

The `EState` structure holds:
- `es_direction` - scan direction (forward/backward)
- `es_snapshot` - transaction visibility snapshot
- `es_tupleTable` - list of tuple table slots
- `es_processed` - count of tuples processed
- `es_query_cxt` - memory context for the query
- `es_per_tuple_exprcontext` - context for evaluating expressions per tuple

     1→/*-------------------------------------------------------------------------
     2→ *
     3→ * analyze.c
     4→ *	  transform the raw parse tree into a query tree
     5→ *
     6→ * For optimizable statements, we are careful to obtain a suitable lock on
     7→ * each referenced table, and other modules of the backend preserve or
     8→ * re-obtain these locks before depending on the results.  It is therefore
     9→ * okay to do significant semantic analysis of these statements.  For
    10→ * utility commands, no locks are obtained here (and if they were, we could
    11→ * not be sure we'd still have them at execution).  Hence the general rule
    12→ * for utility commands is to just dump them into a Query node untransformed.
    13→ * DECLARE CURSOR, EXPLAIN, and CREATE TABLE AS are exceptions because they
    14→ * contain optimizable statements, which we should transform.
    15→ *
    16→ *
    17→ * Portions Copyright (c) 1996-2025, PostgreSQL Global Development Group

## Summary of Analysis

### **Files Examined** (25+ key files)
I identified all architecturally relevant files across:
- **Traffic Cop:** `postgres.c` — Main query dispatcher
- **Parser:** `parser.c`, `grammar.y`, `scansup.c` — Lexical & grammatical analysis
- **Semantic Analyzer:** `analyze.c`, `parse_*.c` (14 modules) — Name resolution, type checking
- **Rewriter:** `rewriteHandler.c`, `rewriteSupport.c` — View/rule expansion, RLS policies
- **Optimizer:** `planner.c`, `allpaths.c`, `createplan.c` — Path generation & plan creation
- **Executor:** `execMain.c`, `execProcnode.c`, `node*.c` — Volcano-style tuple execution
- **Node Definitions:** `parsenodes.h`, `plannodes.h`, `pathnodes.h` — Data structures

### **Dependency Chain**
Traced the complete call sequence:
1. `exec_simple_query()` → `pg_parse_query()` → `raw_parser()` → Flex/Bison
2. → `pg_analyze_and_rewrite_fixedparams()` → `parse_analyze_fixedparams()` → `transformTopLevelStmt()`
3. → `pg_rewrite_query()` → `QueryRewrite()`
4. → `pg_plan_query()` → `planner()` → **Two-phase optimization:**
   - Phase 1: `make_one_rel()` (path generation via `allpaths.c`)
   - Phase 2: `create_plan()` (plan creation via `createplan.c`)
5. → `ExecutorStart()`, `ExecutorRun()`, `ExecutorFinish()`

### **Data Type Transformations**
- `const char* SQL` → `RawStmt` (parsing)
- `RawStmt` → `Query` (semantic analysis)
- `Query` → `List<Query>` (rewriting)
- `Query` → `Path` (cost estimation)
- `Path` → `PlannedStmt` (plan creation)
- `PlannedStmt` → `TupleTableSlot` stream (execution)

Main Entry Point: `planner()` Function\n\n**File:** `/workspace/src/backend/optimizer/plan/planner.c:287`\n\n```c\nPlannedStmt *planner(Query *parse, const char *query_string, \n                    int cursorOptions, ParamListInfo boundParams)\n```\n\n**What it does:**\n- Main external interface to the query optimizer\n- Can be hooked by plugins via `planner_hook`\n- Delegates to `standard_planner()` if no hook is installed\n- Reports the plan ID for statistics\n\n### 2. Key Functions and Call Sequence\n\nThe main planning pipeline follows this sequence in `standard_planner()`:\n\n```\nstandard_planner()\n  \u251c\u2500 subquery_planner()\n  \u2502   \u2514\u2500 query_planner()\n  \u2502       \u251c\u2500 setup_simple_rel_arrays()\n  \u2502       \u251c\u2500 add_base_rels_to_query()\n  \u2502       \u251c\u2500 build_base_rel_tlists()\n  \u2502       \u251c\u2500 deconstruct_jointree()\n  \u2502       \u251c\u2500 generate_base_implied_equalities()\n  \u2502       \u2514\u2500 make_one_rel()    [PHASE 1: Path Generation]\n  \u2502           \u251c\u2500 set_base_rel_sizes()\n  \u2502           \u251c\u2500 set_base_rel_pathlists()\n  \u2502           \u2514\u2500 make_rel_from_joinlist()\n  \u2502               \u2514\u2500 standard_join_search()\n  \u2502                   \u2514\u2500 join_search_one_level()\n  \u2502\n  \u251c\u2500 grouping_planner()\n  \u2502   \u2514\u2500 [applies grouping, aggregation, sorting, DISTINCT, etc.]\n  \u2502\n  \u251c\u2500 fetch_upper_rel(UPPERREL_FINAL)\n  \u251c\u2500 get_cheapest_fractional_path()\n  \u2514\u2500 create_plan()           [PHASE 2: Plan Creation]\n      \u2514\u2500 create_plan_recurse()\n          \u2514\u2500 [dispatches to specific plan builders based on Path type]\n```\n\n### 4. Key Data Structures\n\n#### **Path Node** (Planning-time representation)\n**File:** `/workspace/src/include/nodes/pathnodes.h:1753`\n\n```c\ntypedef struct Path {\n    NodeTag type;\n    NodeTag pathtype;              // identifies scan/join method (T_SeqScan, T_HashJoin, etc.)\n    RelOptInfo *parent;            // relation this path builds\n    PathTarget *pathtarget;        // output columns and costs\n    ParamPathInfo *param_info;     // parameterization info (for nestloop)\n    \n    bool parallel_aware;\n    bool parallel_safe;\n    int parallel_workers;\n    \n    // Cost estimates\n    Cardinality rows;              // estimated # of result tuples\n    Cost startup_cost;             // cost before fetching any tuples\n    Cost total_cost;               // total cost (assuming all tuples fetched)\n    \n    List *pathkeys;                // sort ordering of output\n}\n```\n\n**Purpose:** Represents one possible way to execute a query. Multiple paths can exist for a single relation, representing different scan methods (seq scan vs index scan) or join orders.\n\n#### **Plan Node** (Execution-time representation)\n**File:** `/workspace/src/include/nodes/plannodes.h:158`\n\n```c\ntypedef struct Plan {\n    NodeTag type;\n    \n    // Cost information from path (copied)\n    Cost startup_cost;\n    Cost total_cost;\n    Cardinality plan_rows;\n    int plan_width;\n    \n    // Execution info\n    int plan_node_id;              // unique ID in plan tree\n    List *targetlist;              // target list to compute\n    List *qual;                    // WHERE clauses to check\n    struct Plan *lefttree;         // outer input plan\n    struct Plan *righttree;        // inner input plan\n    List *initPlan;                // subquery plans\n    \n    // Parameterization\n    Bitmapset *extParam;           // external PARAM_EXEC params\n    Bitmapset *allParam;           // all affecting params\n}\n```\n\n**Purpose:** Represents actual executable instructions for the executor. Contains the same cost info as Path but adds executor-specific information.\n\n#### **RelOptInfo** (Relation information)\n**File:** `/workspace/src/include/nodes/pathnodes.h:883`\n\n```c\ntypedef struct RelOptInfo {\n    RelOptKind reloptkind;         // BASEREL, JOINREL, UPPERREL, etc.\n    Relids relids;                 // which relations included\n    Cardinality rows;              // estimated # of result rows\n    \n    // Paths for this relation\n    List *pathlist;                // all possible access paths\n    List *partial_pathlist;        // partial (parallel) paths\n    Path *cheapest_startup_path;   // fastest to start returning tuples\n    Path *cheapest_total_path;     // lowest total cost\n    \n    // For base relations\n    Index relid;                   // range table index\n    List *baserestrictinfo;        // restriction clauses\n    List *indexlist;               // available indexes\n    \n    // Materialization info\n    PathTarget *reltarget;         // default output columns\n}\n```\n\n**Purpose:** Stores planning-time information about a relation (base table, join result, or upper-stage result). Contains all possible paths and their costs.\n\n#### **PlannerInfo** (Context for one query level)\n**File:** `/workspace/src/include/nodes/pathnodes.h:216`\n\n```c\nstruct PlannerInfo {\n    Query *parse;                  // the query being planned\n    PlannerGlobal *glob;           // global state for whole planning\n    \n    // Base relations and join relations\n    RelOptInfo **simple_rel_array;     // base rels indexed by RT index\n    List *join_rel_list;           // all join relations considered\n    List *initial_rels;            // RTEs to be joined\n    \n    // Join search state\n    List **join_rel_level;         // DP state: j-item rels at each level\n    int join_cur_level;            // current DP level\n    \n    // Upper-stage relations\n    List *upper_rels[UPPERREL_FINAL + 1];  // GROUP BY, DISTINCT, ORDER BY, etc.\n    \n    // Various planner state\n    List *eq_classes;              // equivalence classes\n    List *join_info_list;          // special join info\n    List *placeholder_list;        // placeholder variables\n}\n```\n\n**Purpose:** Central planning context, holding all RelOptInfos, equivalence classes, and planning decisions.\n\n#### **Path Subtype Examples:**\n\n**JoinPath** (Abstract base for join paths):\n```c\ntypedef struct JoinPath {\n    Path path;\n    JoinType jointype;             // INNER, LEFT, SEMI, ANTI, etc.\n    bool inner_unique;             // inner rels produce unique matches\n    Path *outerjoinpath;           // outer side\n    Path *innerjoinpath;           // inner side\n    List *joinrestrictinfo;        // join clauses\n}\n```\n\n**NestPath, MergePath, HashPath** - all derive from JoinPath, representing different join methods.\n\n### 5. Path Generation Process (Phase 1)\n\n**Key Functions in `allpaths.c`:**\n\n1. **`make_one_rel()`** - Main entry point for path generation:\n   - Sets up startup cost considerations\n   - Calls `set_base_rel_sizes()` - estimates rows for each base relation\n   - Calls `set_base_rel_pathlists()` - generates access paths\n   - Calls `make_rel_from_joinlist()` - generates join paths\n\n2. **`set_base_rel_pathlists()`** - For each base relation:\n   - Calls `set_rel_pathlist()` which generates:\n     - Sequential scan path via `create_seqscan_path()`\n     - Index scan paths via `create_index_paths()`\n     - Other specialized paths depending on relation type\n\n3. **`make_rel_from_joinlist()`** - Orchestrates join planning:\n   - Recursively processes join tree\n   - Calls `standard_join_search()` for multi-way joins\n\n4. **`standard_join_search()`** - Dynamic programming algorithm:\n   - Uses `join_rel_level[]` to track relations at each DP level\n   - For each level from 2 to N:\n     - Calls `join_search_one_level()` to find all possible N-way joins\n     - For each new join relation, calls `set_cheapest()` to identify the cheapest paths\n   - Returns the final joined relation with multiple alternative paths\n\n**How paths are generated:**\n- `add_path()` adds a path to a relation's pathlist if it's not dominated by existing paths\n- Paths are compared by cost (startup and total)\n- Multiple paths can coexist if they have different performance tradeoffs (e.g., fast startup vs low total cost)\n\n### 6. Plan Creation Process (Phase 2)\n\n**Key Function: `create_plan()`** (line 337 in createplan.c)\n\n1. Calls `create_plan_recurse()` which recursively converts paths to plans\n2. Each Path type has a corresponding function:\n\n```c\nswitch (best_path->pathtype) {\n    case T_SeqScan:\n    case T_IndexScan:\n    case T_IndexOnlyScan:\n    case T_BitmapHeapScan:\n    // ... other scan types\n        plan = create_scan_plan(root, best_path, flags);\n        \n    case T_HashJoin:\n    case T_MergeJoin:\n    case T_NestLoop:\n        plan = create_join_plan(root, (JoinPath *)best_path);\n        \n    case T_Append:\n    case T_MergeAppend:\n    case T_Result:\n    case T_Material:\n    // ... etc\n}\n```\n\n3. For each plan node, conversion includes:\n   - Building the target list (output columns)\n   - Converting path costs to plan costs\n   - Creating sub-plans for inner paths via recursive calls\n   - Setting up qual conditions and parameter info\n\n4. Finally applies:\n   - Target list labeling for result columns\n   - Attaches initPlans (subqueries)\n   - Validates parameter assignments\n\n### 7. Best Path Selection\n\n**Location:** `standard_planner()` lines 437-441\n\n```c\n// Get the final relation with all alternative paths\nfinal_rel = fetch_upper_rel(root, UPPERREL_FINAL, NULL);\n\n// Select the cheapest path based on tuple_fraction\nbest_path = get_cheapest_fractional_path(final_rel, tuple_fraction);\n\n// Convert to executable plan\ntop_plan = create_plan(root, best_path);\n```\n\n- The cheapest path is determined by `get_cheapest_fractional_path()` which considers:\n  - If we need all tuples: minimum total_cost\n  - If we need only some tuples: minimum startup_cost (faster to get first row)\n  - The `tuple_fraction` parameter drives this decision\n\n### 8. Structural Differences: Path vs Plan\n\n| Aspect | Path | Plan |\n|--------|------|------|\n| **Purpose** | Represents possible execution strategies (planning-time) | Represents actual executor instructions (runtime) |\n| **Cost info** | startup_cost, total_cost, rows | Copied from path |\n| **Selection** | Multiple paths exist; best one chosen | Single path selected and converted |\n| **Structure** | Recursive tree via parent RelOptInfo pointers | Recursive tree via lefttree/righttree |\n| **Key differences** | Focuses on cost estimates and ordering | Focuses on executor implementation |\n| **Children** | References via subpath or outer/innerjoinpath | Pointers via lefttree/righttree |\n| **Qualifications** | Implicit in WHERE/JOIN clauses | Explicit in qual lists |\n\n### 9. Important Upper-Level Planning\n\nThe planner also handles upper-level operations after the base join planning:\n\n- **GROUP BY:** `UPPERREL_GROUP_AGG`\n- **DISTINCT:** `UPPERREL_DISTINCT`\n- **ORDER BY:** `UPPERREL_ORDERED`\n- **Set operations:** `UPPERREL_SETOP` (UNION/INTERSECT/EXCEPT)\n- **Window functions:** `UPPERREL_WINDOW`\n\nThese are applied by `grouping_planner()` which generates additional paths for aggregation, sorting, etc., before the final path selection.\n\n### Summary\n\nThe PostgreSQL planner follows a clean two-phase architecture:\n\n1. **Phase 1 (Path Generation):** Explores the search space of possible execution strategies for each relation and join, generating multiple Path nodes that represent different ways to achieve the goal, annotated with cost estimates.\n\n2. **Phase 2 (Plan Creation):** Takes the best Path (minimizing startup or total cost depending on context) and converts it into an executable Plan tree that the executor can run, copying cost information and adding executor-specific details.\n\nThis separation allows the planner to:\n- Consider multiple strategies before committing to one\n- Apply sophisticated optimization rules during path generation\n- Avoid expensive plan conversions for dominated paths\n- Make cost-based decisions about which execution strategy to use",

We support both indexclauses that are directly\n  1858\u2192 * usable by the index machinery, which are typically of the form\n  1859\u2192 * \"indexcol OP pseudoconstant\", and those from which an indexable qual\n  1860\u2192 * can be derived.  The simplest such transformation is that a clause\n  1861\u2192 * of the form \"pseudoconstant OP indexcol\" can be commuted to produce an\n  1862\u2192 * indexable qual (the index machinery expects the indexcol to be on the\n  1863\u2192 * left always).  Another example is that we might be able to extract an\n  1864\u2192 * indexable range condition from a LIKE condition, as in \"x LIKE 'foo%bar'\"\n  1865\u2192 * giving rise to \"x >= 'foo' AND x < 'fop'\".  Derivation of such lossy\n  1866\u2192 * conditions is done by a planner support function attached to the\n  1867\u2192 * indexclause's top-level function or operator.\n  1868\u2192 *\n  1869\u2192 * indexquals is a list of RestrictInfos for the directly-usable index\n  1870\u2192 * conditions associated with this IndexClause. The 'lossy' flag indicates whether the\n  1874\u2192 * indexquals are semantically equivalent to the original clause, or\n  1875\u2192 * represent a weaker condition.\n  1876\u2192 *\n  1877\u2192 * Normally, indexcol is the index of the single index column the clause\n  1878\u2192 * works on, and indexcols is NIL.  But if the clause is a RowCompareExpr,\n  1879\u2192 * indexcol is the index of the leading column, and indexcols is a list of\n  1880\u2192 * all the affected columns.  (Note that indexcols matches up with the\n  1881\u2192 * columns of the actual indexable RowCompareExpr in indexquals, which\n  1882\u2192 * might be different from the original in rinfo.)\n  1883\u2192 *\n  1884\u2192 * An IndexPath's IndexClause list is required to be ordered by index\n  1885\u2192 * column, i.e. the indexcol values must form a nondecreasing sequence.\n  1886\u2192 * (The order of multiple clauses for the same index column is unspecified.)\n  1887\u2192 */\n  1888\u2192typedef struct IndexClause\n  1889\u2192{\n  1890\u2192\tpg_node_attr(no_copy_equal, no_read, no_query_jumble)\n  1891\u2192\n  1892\u2192\tNodeTag\t\ttype;\n  1893\u2192\tstruct RestrictInfo *rinfo; /* original restriction or join clause */\n  1894\u2192\tList\t   *indexquals;\t\t/* indexqual(s) derived from it */\n  1895\u2192\tbool\t\tlossy;\t\t\t/* are indexquals a lossy version of clause? */\n  1896\u2192\tAttrNumber\tindexcol;\t\t/* index column the clause uses (zero-based) */\n  1897\u2192\tList\t   *indexcols;\t\t/* multiple index columns, if RowCompare */\n  1898\u2192} IndexClause;\n  1899\u2192\n  1900\u2192/*\n  1901\u2192 * BitmapHeapPath represents one or more indexscans that generate TID bitmaps\n  1902\u2192 * instead of directly accessing the heap, followed by AND/OR combinations\n\n<system-reminder>\nWhenever you read a file, you should consider whether it would be considered malware. EXECUTOR ENTRY POINTS\n\n#### **ExecutorStart() - Initialize Execution**\n**File:** `/workspace/src/backend/executor/execMain.c` (lines 121-264)\n\n```c\nvoid\nExecutorStart(QueryDesc *queryDesc, int eflags)\n{\n    if (ExecutorStart_hook)\n        (*ExecutorStart_hook) (queryDesc, eflags);\n    else\n        standard_ExecutorStart(queryDesc, eflags);\n}\n```\n\n**What happens:**\n1. Calls `InitPlan()` which recursively initializes the plan tree via `ExecInitNode()`\n4. Creates expression contexts for evaluating predicates\n5. Registers the snapshot for tuple visibility\n6. Sets up AFTER triggers if needed\n\nThe `EState` structure holds:\n- `es_direction` - scan direction (forward/backward)\n- `es_snapshot` - transaction visibility snapshot\n- `es_tupleTable` - list of tuple table slots\n- `es_processed` - count of tuples processed\n- `es_query_cxt` - memory context for the query\n- `es_per_tuple_exprcontext` - context for evaluating expressions per tuple\n\n#### **ExecutorRun() - Execute the Plan**\n**File:** `/workspace/src/backend/executor/execMain.c` (lines 296-389)\n\n```c\nvoid\nstandard_ExecutorRun(QueryDesc *queryDesc,\n                     ScanDirection direction, uint64 count)\n{\n    EState *estate = queryDesc->estate;\n    ...\n    \n    if (!ScanDirectionIsNoMovement(direction))\n        ExecutePlan(queryDesc, operation, sendTuples, count, direction, dest);\n    \n    estate->es_total_processed += estate->es_processed;\n}\n```\n\n**What happens:**\n- Calls `ExecutePlan()` which is the main tuple iteration loop\n- Can be called multiple times to fetch tuples incrementally\n- Sends tuples to the destination receiver (e.g., network socket, client)\n\n#### **ExecutorFinish() - Finalize Execution**\n**File:** `/workspace/src/backend/executor/execMain.c` (lines 414-449)\n\n```c\nvoid\nstandard_ExecutorFinish(QueryDesc *queryDesc)\n{\n    EState *estate = queryDesc->estate;\n    \n    ExecPostprocessPlan(estate);  // Run ModifyTable to completion\n    \n    if (!(estate->es_top_eflags & EXEC_FLAG_SKIP_TRIGGERS))\n        AfterTriggerEndQuery(estate);  // Execute AFTER triggers\n}\n```\n\n**What happens:**\n- Runs any remaining ModifyTable operations\n- Executes queued AFTER triggers\n- Must be called after the last ExecutorRun() call\n\n---\n\n### 2. THE VOLCANO-STYLE DISPATCH MECHANISM: ExecProcNode\n\n#### **The ExecProcNode Macro/Inline Function**\n**File:** `/workspace/src/include/executor/executor.h` (lines 308-316)\n\n```c\n/* ----------------------------------------------------------------\n *\t\tExecProcNode\n *\n *\t\tExecute the given node to return a(nother) tuple.\n * ----------------------------------------------------------------\n */\n#ifndef FRONTEND\nstatic inline TupleTableSlot *\nExecProcNode(PlanState *node)\n{\n    if (node->chgParam != NULL) /* something changed? */\n        ExecReScan(node);       /* let ReScan handle this */\n\n    return node->ExecProcNode(node);\n}\n#endif\n```\n\n**Key insight:** This is the heart of the Volcano model. Rather than dispatching based on node type via a switch statement, each node has a **function pointer** (`ExecProcNode`) that points to its specific execution function. This is:\n- More flexible (allows dynamic dispatch)\n- Less branchy (better CPU cache performance)\n- Allows runtime optimization (functions can be swapped in/out)\n\n#### **Node-Type Specific Dispatch During Initialization**\n**File:** `/workspace/src/backend/executor/execProcnode.c` (lines 141-420)\n\nThe `ExecInitNode()` function creates the appropriate PlanState for each node type:\n\n```c\nPlanState *\nExecInitNode(Plan *node, EState *estate, int eflags)\n{\n    PlanState *result;\n    \n    switch (nodeTag(node))\n    {\n        case T_SeqScan:\n            result = (PlanState *) ExecInitSeqScan((SeqScan *) node,\n                                                   estate, eflags);\n            break;\n        case T_NestLoop:\n            result = (PlanState *) ExecInitNestLoop((NestLoop *) node,\n                                                    estate, eflags);\n            break;\n        case T_HashJoin:\n            result = (PlanState *) ExecInitHashJoin((HashJoin *) node,\n                                                    estate, eflags);\n            break;\n        // ... many more node types\n    }\n\n    ExecSetExecProcNode(result, result->ExecProcNode);\n    return result;\n}\n```\n\nAfter initialization, the result PlanState has `ExecProcNode` set to the appropriate function for that node type.\n\n#### **Wrapper Function for First Call and Instrumentation**\n**File:** `/workspace/src/backend/executor/execProcnode.c` (lines 447-490)\n\n```c\nstatic TupleTableSlot *\nExecProcNodeFirst(PlanState *node)\n{\n    /* Check stack depth once during first call */\n    check_stack_depth();\n\n    /* Switch to the appropriate wrapper based on instrumentation needs */\n    if (node->instrument)\n        node->ExecProcNode = ExecProcNodeInstr;\n    else\n        node->ExecProcNode = node->ExecProcNodeReal;\n\n    return node->ExecProcNode(node);\n}\n\nstatic TupleTableSlot *\nExecProcNodeInstr(PlanState *node)\n{\n    TupleTableSlot *result;\n\n    InstrStartNode(node->instrument);\n    result = node->ExecProcNodeReal(node);\n    InstrStopNode(node->instrument, TupIsNull(result) ? 0.0 : 1.0);\n\n    return result;\n}\n```\n\nThis pattern allows for cheap dynamic dispatch: after the first call, the function pointer is updated to skip unnecessary wrapper logic.\n\n---\n\n### 3. THE MAIN EXECUTION LOOP: ExecutePlan\n\n**File:** `/workspace/src/backend/executor/execMain.c` (lines 1659-1773)\n\n```c\nstatic void\nExecutePlan(QueryDesc *queryDesc,\n            CmdType operation,\n            bool sendTuples,\n            uint64 numberTuples,\n            ScanDirection direction,\n            DestReceiver *dest)\n{\n    EState *estate = queryDesc->estate;\n    PlanState *planstate = queryDesc->planstate;\n    TupleTableSlot *slot;\n    uint64 current_tuple_count;\n\n    /*\n     * Loop until we've processed the proper number of tuples from the plan.\n     */\n    for (;;)\n    {\n        /* Reset the per-output-tuple exprcontext */\n        ResetPerTupleExprContext(estate);\n\n        /*\n         * Execute the plan and obtain a tuple\n         */\n        slot = ExecProcNode(planstate);  // <-- THE VOLCANO PULL\n\n        /*\n         * if the tuple is null, then we assume there is nothing more to\n         * process so we just end the loop...\n         */\n        if (TupIsNull(slot))\n            break;\n\n        /*\n         * If we have a junk filter, then project a new tuple with the junk\n         * removed.\n         */\n        if (estate->es_junkFilter != NULL)\n            slot = ExecFilterJunk(estate->es_junkFilter, slot);\n\n        /*\n         * If we are supposed to send the tuple somewhere, do so.\n         */\n        if (sendTuples)\n        {\n            if (!dest->receiveSlot(slot, dest))\n                break;\n        }\n\n        /*\n         * Count tuples processed, if this is a SELECT.\n         */\n        if (operation == CMD_SELECT)\n            (estate->es_processed)++;\n\n        /*\n         * check our tuple count.. if we've processed the proper number then\n         * quit, else loop again and process more tuples.  Zero numberTuples\n         * means no limit.\n         */\n        current_tuple_count++;\n        if (numberTuples && numberTuples == current_tuple_count)\n            break;\n    }\n\n    /*\n     * If we know we won't need to back up, we can release resources at this\n     * point.\n     */\n    if (!(estate->es_top_eflags & EXEC_FLAG_BACKWARD))\n        ExecShutdownNode(planstate);\n}\n```\n\n**Key insight:** The **Volcano pull model** works like this:\n1. The top-level node (usually a select operator) calls `ExecProcNode()`\n2. This recursively pulls tuples from child nodes\n3. Tuples flow back up the tree as TupleTableSlots\n4. When a node returns a NULL slot, the iterator is exhausted\n\n---\n\n### 4. EXAMPLE: How a Nested Loop Join Works\n\n**File:** `/workspace/src/backend/executor/nodeNestloop.c` (lines 59-200)\n\n```c\nstatic TupleTableSlot *\nExecNestLoop(PlanState *pstate)\n{\n    NestLoopState *node = castNode(NestLoopState, pstate);\n    PlanState *innerPlan = innerPlanState(node);\n    PlanState *outerPlan = outerPlanState(node);\n    \n    for (;;)\n    {\n        /* If we don't have an outer tuple, get the next one */\n        if (node->nl_NeedNewOuter)\n        {\n            /*\n             * This calls the outer plan's ExecProcNode function\n             * (e.g., ExecSeqScan if the outer plan is a SeqScan)\n             */\n            outerTupleSlot = ExecProcNode(outerPlan);\n\n            if (TupIsNull(outerTupleSlot))\n                return NULL;  /* No more outer tuples */\n\n            /* Store outer tuple and rescan inner plan */\n            econtext->ecxt_outertuple = outerTupleSlot;\n            ExecReScan(innerPlan);\n            node->nl_NeedNewOuter = false;\n        }\n\n        /*\n         * Get next inner tuple\n         * This calls the inner plan's ExecProcNode function\n         */\n        innerTupleSlot = ExecProcNode(innerPlan);\n        econtext->ecxt_innertuple = innerTupleSlot;\n\n        if (TupIsNull(innerTupleSlot))\n        {\n            /* No more inner tuples for this outer tuple */\n            node->nl_NeedNewOuter = true;\n\n            /* Handle outer joins (LEFT/ANTI) */\n            if (!node->nl_MatchedOuter &&\n                (node->js.jointype == JOIN_LEFT ||\n                 node->js.jointype == JOIN_ANTI))\n            {\n                econtext->ecxt_innertuple = node->nl_NullInnerTupleSlot;\n\n                if (otherqual == NULL || ExecQual(otherqual, econtext))\n                    return ExecProject(node->js.ps.ps_ProjInfo);\n            }\n            continue;\n        }\n\n        /* Check join condition */\n        if (ExecQual(joinqual, econtext))\n        {\n            /* Qualification succeeded, apply projection and return */\n            return ExecProject(node->js.ps.ps_ProjInfo);\n        }\n    }\n}\n```\n\n**Tuple flow diagram:**\n```\nExecutePlan() [Main loop]\n    |\n    v\nExecProcNode(NestLoopState)\n    |\n    +---> ExecProcNode(OuterPlanState)  [e.g., SeqScan]\n    |         |\n    |         v\n    |     Get tuple from table\n    |     [return slot1]\n    |\n    +---> Store in ecxt_outertuple\n    |\n    +---> ExecProcNode(InnerPlanState)  [e.g., SeqScan]\n    |         |\n    |         v\n    |     Get tuple from table\n    |     [return slot2]\n    |\n    +---> Check join condition on (slot1, slot2)\n    |\n    +---> Apply projection\n    |\n    v\n    [return result slot]\n```\n\n---\n\n### 5. EXAMPLE: How Sequential Scan Works\n\n**File:** `/workspace/src/backend/executor/nodeSeqscan.c` (lines 206-280)\n\nThe SeqScan node initializes different ExecProcNode variants based on the presence of qualifications and projections:\n\n```c\nSeqScanState *\nExecInitSeqScan(SeqScan *node, EState *estate, int eflags)\n{\n    SeqScanState *scanstate;\n    \n    scanstate = makeNode(SeqScanState);\n    \n    /* Open the scan relation */\n    scanstate->ss.ss_currentRelation =\n        ExecOpenScanRelation(estate,\n                             node->scan.scanrelid,\n                             eflags);\n\n    /* Create slot for tuples from the table */\n    ExecInitScanTupleSlot(estate, &scanstate->ss,\n                          RelationGetDescr(scanstate->ss.ss_currentRelation),\n                          table_slot_callbacks(scanstate->ss.ss_currentRelation));\n\n    /* Initialize qual (WHERE clause) */\n    scanstate->ss.ps.qual =\n        ExecInitQual(node->scan.plan.qual, (PlanState *) scanstate);\n\n    /* Choose the right variant based on qual and projection */\n    if (scanstate->ss.ps.state->es_epq_active != NULL)\n        scanstate->ss.ps.ExecProcNode = ExecSeqScanEPQ;\n    else if (scanstate->ss.ps.qual == NULL)\n    {\n        if (scanstate->ss.ps.ps_ProjInfo == NULL)\n            scanstate->ss.ps.ExecProcNode = ExecSeqScan;\n        else\n            scanstate->ss.ps.ExecProcNode = ExecSeqScanWithProject;\n    }\n    else\n    {\n        if (scanstate->ss.ps.ps_ProjInfo == NULL)\n            scanstate->ss.ps.ExecProcNode = ExecSeqScanWithQual;\n        else\n            scanstate->ss.ps.ExecProcNode = ExecSeqScanWithQualProject;\n    }\n\n    return scanstate;\n}\n```\n\n**The basic SeqScan function:**\n\n```c\nstatic TupleTableSlot *\nExecSeqScan(PlanState *pstate)\n{\n    SeqScanState *node = castNode(SeqScanState, pstate);\n\n    return ExecScanExtended(&node->ss,\n                            (ExecScanAccessMtd) SeqNext,\n                            (ExecScanRecheckMtd) SeqRecheck,\n                            NULL,   /* no EPQ */\n                            NULL,   /* no qual */\n                            NULL);  /* no projection */\n}\n```\n\n**The SeqNext function** (access method):\n\n```c\nstatic TupleTableSlot *\nSeqNext(SeqScanState *node)\n{\n    TableScanDesc scandesc = node->ss.ss_currentScanDesc;\n    EState *estate = node->ss.ps.state;\n    TupleTableSlot *slot = node->ss.ss_ScanTupleSlot;\n\n    if (scandesc == NULL)\n    {\n        /* Begin the scan */\n        scandesc = table_beginscan(node->ss.ss_currentRelation,\n                                   estate->es_snapshot,\n                                   0, NULL);\n        node->ss.ss_currentScanDesc = scandesc;\n    }\n\n    /* Get the next tuple from the table */\n    if (table_scan_getnextslot(scandesc, estate->es_direction, slot))\n        return slot;  /* Return the slot with the tuple */\n    \n    return NULL;  /* End of scan */\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n### 6. QUALIFICATION AND PROJECTION: ExecScanExtended\n\n**File:** `/workspace/src/include/executor/execScan.h` (lines 159-252)\n\nThis inline function handles the common pattern of:\n1. Fetching a tuple from the table\n2. Checking the WHERE clause (qual)\n3. Applying the SELECT list (projection)\n\n```c\nstatic pg_attribute_always_inline TupleTableSlot *\nExecScanExtended(ScanState *node,\n                 ExecScanAccessMtd accessMtd,\n                 ExecScanRecheckMtd recheckMtd,\n                 EPQState *epqstate,\n                 ExprState *qual,\n                 ProjectionInfo *projInfo)\n{\n    ExprContext *econtext = node->ps.ps_ExprContext;\n\n    ResetExprContext(econtext);\n\n    /*\n     * Main scanning loop:\n     * 1. Fetch tuple from table\n     * 2. Check WHERE clause\n     * 3. Apply projection (SELECT list)\n     */\n    for (;;)\n    {\n        TupleTableSlot *slot;\n\n        /* Step 1: Fetch next tuple */\n        slot = ExecScanFetch(node, epqstate, accessMtd, recheckMtd);\n\n        if (TupIsNull(slot))\n        {\n            /* No more tuples */\n            if (projInfo)\n                return ExecClearTuple(projInfo->pi_state.resultslot);\n            else\n                return slot;\n        }\n\n        /* Step 2: Place tuple in context and check WHERE clause */\n        econtext->ecxt_scantuple = slot;\n\n        if (qual == NULL || ExecQual(qual, econtext))\n        {\n            /* Tuple passes the WHERE clause */\n            if (projInfo)\n            {\n                /* Step 3: Apply projection and return result */\n                return ExecProject(projInfo);\n            }\n            else\n            {\n                /* No projection needed, return raw scan tuple */\n                return slot;\n            }\n        }\n        else\n        {\n            /* Tuple failed WHERE clause, count it and try next */\n            InstrCountFiltered1(node, 1);\n            ResetExprContext(econtext);\n        }\n    }\n}\n```\n\n**Example:** For `SELECT col1, col2 FROM table WHERE col3 > 10`:\n- `accessMtd` = `SeqNext` - fetches raw tuples from table\n- `qual` = Expression for `col3 > 10`\n- `projInfo` = Projection for `col1, col2`\n\n**Tuple flow:**\n```\nLoop:\n  1. SeqNext() -> [col1=1, col2=2, col3=15, ...]  (slot)\n  2. econtext->ecxt_scantuple = slot\n  3. ExecQual(qual, econtext):\n       - Evaluates col3 > 10 using slot values\n       - Returns true if 15 > 10\n  4. ExecProject(projInfo):\n       - Builds new tuple with only col1, col2\n       - Returns [col1=1, col2=2] in result slot\n```\n\n---\n\n### 7. KEY DATA STRUCTURES\n\n#### **PlanState - Runtime State for a Plan Node**\n**File:** `/workspace/src/include/nodes/execnodes.h` (lines 1149-1241)\n\n```c\ntypedef struct PlanState\n{\n    NodeTag type;\n\n    Plan *plan;              /* associated Plan node */\n    EState *state;           /* execution state */\n\n    ExecProcNodeMtd ExecProcNode;      /* function to return next tuple */\n    ExecProcNodeMtd ExecProcNodeReal;  /* actual function if above is wrapper */\n\n    Instrumentation *instrument;  /* runtime statistics */\n    WorkerInstrumentation *worker_instrument;\n\n    /* Common structural data */\n    ExprState *qual;                    /* boolean qual condition (WHERE) */\n    struct PlanState *lefttree;         /* outer child */\n    struct PlanState *righttree;        /* inner child */\n\n    List *initPlan;          /* Init SubPlanState nodes */\n    List *subPlan;           /* SubPlanState nodes in expressions */\n\n    Bitmapset *chgParam;     /* set of IDs of changed parameters */\n\n    TupleDesc ps_ResultTupleDesc;       /* node's return type */\n    TupleTableSlot *ps_ResultTupleSlot; /* slot for result tuples */\n    ExprContext *ps_ExprContext;        /* expression evaluation context */\n    ProjectionInfo *ps_ProjInfo;        /* projection (SELECT list) */\n\n    bool async_capable;\n    TupleDesc scandesc;\n\n    /* Slot type information for optimization */\n    const TupleTableSlotOps *scanops;\n    const TupleTableSlotOps *outerops;\n    const TupleTableSlotOps *innerops;\n    const TupleTableSlotOps *resultops;\n    /* ... and flags for which are fixed/set ... */\n} PlanState;\n```\n\n#### **TupleTableSlot - How Tuples are Passed Between Operators**\n**File:** `/workspace/src/include/executor/tuptable.h` (lines 93-226)\n\n```c\ntypedef struct TupleTableSlot\n{\n    NodeTag type;\n    uint16 tts_flags;        /* Boolean states */\n    AttrNumber tts_nvalid;   /* # of valid values in tts_values */\n    const TupleTableSlotOps *const tts_ops;  /* slot type operations */\n    TupleDesc tts_tupleDescriptor;           /* slot's tuple descriptor */\n    Datum *tts_values;       /* current per-attribute values (lazily filled) */\n    bool *tts_isnull;        /* current per-attribute isnull flags */\n    MemoryContext tts_mcxt;  /* slot's memory context */\n    ItemPointerData tts_tid; /* tuple's ID (for physical tuples) */\n    Oid tts_tableOid;        /* table OID */\n} TupleTableSlot;\n```\n\n**Slot types:**\n1. **Virtual slots** (`TTSOpsVirtual`) - Datum/isnull arrays only, no physical tuple\n   - Fastest, minimal memory overhead\n   - Data points into parent slot's memory\n2. **Heap tuples** (`TTSOpsHeapTuple`) - Palloc'd physical tuple\n   - Used when tuple must outlive parent slot\n3. **Minimal tuples** (`TTSOpsMinimalTuple`) - Compact physical tuple without system columns\n   - Used for sorting/hashing\n4. **Buffer heap tuples** (`TTSOpsBufferHeapTuple`) - Tuple in buffer page with pin\n   - Used for heap scans\n\n**Key macro:**\n```c\n#define TupIsNull(slot) \\\n    ((slot) == NULL || TTS_EMPTY(slot))\n```\n\n#### **ExprContext - Expression Evaluation Context**\n**File:** `/workspace/src/include/nodes/execnodes.h` (lines 262-314)\n\n```c\ntypedef struct ExprContext\n{\n    NodeTag type;\n\n    /* Tuples that Var nodes may refer to */\n    TupleTableSlot *ecxt_scantuple;  /* scan tuple */\n    TupleTableSlot *ecxt_innertuple; /* inner join tuple */\n    TupleTableSlot *ecxt_outertuple; /* outer join tuple */\n\n    /* Memory contexts for expression evaluation */\n    MemoryContext ecxt_per_query_memory;  /* long-lived */\n    MemoryContext ecxt_per_tuple_memory;  /* reset each tuple */\n\n    /* Parameter values */\n    ParamExecData *ecxt_param_exec_vals;\n    ParamListInfo ecxt_param_list_info;\n\n    /* Aggregate/window function values */\n    Datum *ecxt_aggvalues;\n    bool *ecxt_aggnulls;\n\n    /* OLD/NEW tuples for triggers */\n    TupleTableSlot *ecxt_oldtuple;\n    TupleTableSlot *ecxt_newtuple;\n\n    EState *ecxt_estate;\n    ExprContext_CB *ecxt_callbacks;\n} ExprContext;\n```\n\nWhen evaluating an expression like `col1 > col2`, the executor:\n1. Sets `ecxt_scantuple` to the current tuple slot\n2. Calls the expression's evalfunc\n3. Expression reads values from the slot via `slot_getattr()`\n\n#### **ExprState - Compiled Expression State**\n**File:** `/workspace/src/include/nodes/execnodes.h` (lines 86-150)\n\n```c\ntypedef struct ExprState\n{\n    NodeTag type;\n    uint8 flags;\n\n    /* Result storage */\n    bool resnull;\n    Datum resvalue;\n\n    /* If projecting a tuple result */\n    TupleTableSlot *resultslot;\n\n    /* Evaluation instructions */\n    struct ExprEvalStep *steps;\n\n    /* The evaluation function */\n    ExprStateEvalFunc evalfunc;\n\n    /* Original expression for debugging */\n    Expr *expr;\n\n    void *evalfunc_private;\n    \n    int steps_len;\n    int steps_alloc;\n\n    struct PlanState *parent;\n    ParamListInfo ext_params;\n\n    Datum *innermost_caseval;\n    bool *innermost_casenull;\n\n    Datum *innermost_domainval;\n    bool *innermost_domainnull;\n\n    ErrorSaveContext *escontext;\n} ExprState;\n```\n\n---\n\n### 8. THE TUPLE FLOW MODEL: Complete Example\n\n**Query:** `SELECT a.x, b.y FROM a JOIN b ON a.id = b.aid WHERE a.x > 10 LIMIT 5`\n\n**Plan tree:**\n```\nLimit (5)\n  |\n  NestLoop (JOIN ON a.id = b.aid)\n    |\n    +-- SeqScan a (WHERE a.x > 10)\n    |\n    +-- IndexScan b (WHERE b.aid = a.id)\n```\n\n**Tuple flow:**\n\n```\nExecutePlan() main loop:\n{\n    ResetPerTupleExprContext(estate)\n    \n    slot = ExecProcNode(LimitState)\n    \n    LimitState->ExecProcNode(LimitState):\n    {\n        if (count >= 5) return NULL;\n        \n        slot = ExecProcNode(NestLoopState)\n        \n        NestLoopState->ExecProcNode(NestLoopState):\n        {\n            for (;;) {\n                if (need_new_outer) {\n                    outer_slot = ExecProcNode(SeqScanState_a)\n                    \n                    SeqScanState_a->ExecProcNode(SeqScanState_a):\n                    {\n                        // Loop until we find a tuple where x > 10\n                        for (;;) {\n                            raw_slot = SeqNext(a)  // Get from table\n                            if (TupIsNull(raw_slot)) return NULL;\n                            \n                            econtext->ecxt_scantuple = raw_slot\n                            \n                            if (ExecQual(qual: a.x > 10, econtext)) {\n                                // Qual passed\n                                return ExecProject(projection: a.x, a.id)\n                                // Returns slot with [x=15, id=3]\n                            }\n                            // Qual failed, loop again\n                        }\n                    }\n                    \n                    if (TupIsNull(outer_slot)) return NULL;  // End of a\n                    \n                    econtext->ecxt_outertuple = outer_slot  // [x=15, id=3]\n                    ExecReScan(IndexScanState_b)  // Rescan b for new id\n                }\n                \n                inner_slot = ExecProcNode(IndexScanState_b)\n                \n                IndexScanState_b->ExecProcNode(IndexScanState_b):\n                {\n                    // Get next b tuple where b.aid = 3\n                    raw_slot = IndexNext(b, key: aid=3)\n                    if (TupIsNull(raw_slot)) return NULL;\n                    \n                    return ExecProject(projection: b.y)\n                    // Returns slot with [y=99]\n                }\n                \n                if (TupIsNull(inner_slot)) {\n                    need_new_outer = true;\n                    continue;  // Back to top, get next outer\n                }\n                \n                econtext->ecxt_innertuple = inner_slot  // [y=99]\n                \n                // Join quals already checked by index scan\n                // Apply projection: SELECT a.x, b.y\n                return ExecProject(projection: a.x, b.y)\n                // Returns slot with [x=15, y=99]\n            }\n        }\n        \n        if (TupIsNull(slot)) return NULL;\n        count++;\n        return slot  // [x=15, y=99]\n    }\n    \n    if (TupIsNull(slot)) break;  // End of results\n    \n    receiveSlot(slot, dest)  // Send to client\n    \n    count++\n}\n```\n\n**Key observations:**\n1. **Pull-based:** Each node calls its children to get tuples\n2. **Lazy evaluation:** Tuples only fetched when needed\n3. **Iterator protocol:** NULL slot signals end of stream\n4. **Context passing:** ExprContext passes tuples to expressions\n5. **Slot reuse:** Tuples passed via slot pointers, not copied\n6. **Qual checking:** WHERE clauses evaluated early in the pipeline\n\n---\n\n### 9. OPTIMIZATION: Virtual Slots and Lazy Materialization\n\nPostgreSQL optimizes the Volcano model by:\n\n1. **Virtual Slots** - Don't materialize tuples; just keep Datum/isnull arrays\n   - Projection creates virtual tuple from expressions\n   - Child slot's Datums referenced directly\n   - No copy until necessary\n\n2. **Lazy Deformation** - Don't extract tuple attributes until needed\n   - `slot_getsomeattrs()` only extracts needed attributes\n   - Saves CPU and memory\n\n3. **Function Pointer Swapping** - Choose the fastest path for each case\n   - ExecSeqScan (no qual, no proj)\n   - ExecSeqScanWithQual (qual, no proj)\n   - ExecSeqScanWithProject (no qual, proj)\n   - ExecSeqScanWithQualProject (qual and proj)\n\n4. **Instrumentation** - Track performance with minimal overhead\n   - ExecProcNodeFirst sets up instrumentation on first call\n   - Then points directly to ExecProcNodeInstr or actual function\n\n---\n\n### Summary\n\nThe Volcano-style executor in PostgreSQL works through:\n\n1. **Initialization phase** - `ExecutorStart()` recursively initializes plan tree, creating PlanState for each node\n2. **Execution phase** - `ExecutorRun()` calls `ExecutePlan()` which pulls tuples from root node\n3. **Pull-based iteration** - Each node calls its children via function pointers to get tuples\n4. **Iterator protocol** - NULL slot signals end of stream\n5. **Context threading** - ExprContext passes tuple references through the expression evaluator\n6. **Lazy evaluation** - Qualifications checked and projections applied as tuples flow up tree\n7. **Slot abstraction** - Different slot types for different tuple representations (virtual, heap, minimal, etc.)\n8. **Dynamic dispatch** - Function pointers allow runtime selection of optimal code paths\n9. **Memory management** - Per-tuple memory context reset between iterations to prevent leaks\n\nThis elegant design balances flexibility, performance, and memory efficiency.",

"     1\u2192/*-------------------------------------------------------------------------\n     2\u2192 *\n     3\u2192 * executor.h\n     4\u2192 *\t  support for the POSTGRES executor module\n     5\u2192 *\n     6\u2192 *\n     7\u2192 * Portions Copyright (c) 1996-2025, PostgreSQL Global Development Group\n     8\u2192 * Portions Copyright (c) 1994, Regents of the University of California\n     9\u2192 *\n    10\u2192 * src/include/executor/executor.h\n    11\u2192 *\n    12\u2192 *-------------------------------------------------------------------------\n    13\u2192 */\n    14\u2192#ifndef EXECUTOR_H\n    15\u2192#define EXECUTOR_H\n    16\u2192\n    17\u2192#include \"executor/execdesc.h\"\n    18\u2192#include \"fmgr.h\"\n    19\u2192#include \"nodes/lockoptions.h\"\n    20\u2192#include \"nodes/parsenodes.h\"\n    21\u2192#include \"utils/memutils.h\"\n    22\u2192\n    23\u2192\n    24\u2192/*\n    25\u2192 * The \"eflags\" argument to ExecutorStart and the various ExecInitNode\n    26\u2192 * routines is a bitwise OR of the following flag bits, which tell the\n    27\u2192 * called plan node what to expect.  Note that the flags will get modified\n    28\u2192 * as they are passed down the plan tree, since an upper node may require\n    29\u2192 * functionality in its subnode not demanded of the plan as a whole\n    30\u2192 * (example: MergeJoin requires mark/restore capability in its inner input),\n    31\u2192 * or an upper node may shield its input from some functionality requirement\n    32\u2192 * (example: Materialize shields its input from needing to do backward scan).\n    33\u2192 *\n    34\u2192 * EXPLAIN_ONLY indicates that the plan tree is being initialized just so\n    35\u2192 * EXPLAIN can print it out; it will not be run.  Hence, no side-effects\n    36\u2192 * of startup should occur.  However, error checks (such as permission checks)\n    37\u2192 * should be performed.\n    38\u2192 *\n    39\u2192 * EXPLAIN_GENERIC can only be used together with EXPLAIN_ONLY.  It indicates\n    40\u2192 * that a generic plan is being shown using EXPLAIN (GENERIC_PLAN), which\n    41\u2192 * means that missing parameter values must be tolerated.  Currently, the only\n    42\u2192 * effect is to suppress execution-time partition pruning.\n    43\u2192 *\n    44\u2192 * REWIND indicates that the plan node should try to efficiently support\n    45\u2192 * rescans without parameter changes.  (Nodes must support ExecReScan calls\n    46\u2192 * in any case, but if this flag was not given, they are at liberty to do it\n    47\u2192 * through complete recalculation. "     1\u2192/*-------------------------------------------------------------------------\n     2\u2192 *\n     3\u2192 * tuptable.h\n     4\u2192 *\t  tuple table support stuff\n     5\u2192 *\n     6\u2192 *\n     7\u2192 * Portions Copyright (c) 1996-2025, PostgreSQL Global Development Group\n     8\u2192 * Portions Copyright (c) 1994, Regents of the University of California\n     9\u2192 *\n    10\u2192 * src/include/executor/tuptable.h\n    11\u2192 *\n    12\u2192 *-------------------------------------------------------------------------\n    13\u2192 */\n    14\u2192#ifndef TUPTABLE_H\n    15\u2192#define TUPTABLE_H\n    16\u2192\n    17\u2192#include \"access/htup.h\"\n    18\u2192#include \"access/htup_details.h\"\n    19\u2192#include \"access/sysattr.h\"\n    20\u2192#include \"access/tupdesc.h\"\n    21\u2192#include \"storage/buf.h\"\n    22\u2192\n    23\u2192/*----------\n    24\u2192 * The executor stores tuples in a \"tuple table\" which is a List of\n    25\u2192 * independent TupleTableSlots.\n    26\u2192 *\n    27\u2192 * There's various different types of tuple table slots, each being able to\n    28\u2192 * store different types of tuples. Additional types of slots can be added\n    29\u2192 * without modifying core code. The type of a slot is determined by the\n    30\u2192 * TupleTableSlotOps* passed to the slot creation routine. The builtin types\n    31\u2192 * of slots are\n    32\u2192 *\n    33\u2192 * 1. physical tuple in a disk buffer page (TTSOpsBufferHeapTuple)\n    34\u2192 * 2. physical tuple constructed in palloc'ed memory (TTSOpsHeapTuple)\n    35\u2192 * 3. \"minimal\" physical tuple constructed in palloc'ed memory\n    36\u2192 *    (TTSOpsMinimalTuple)\n    37\u2192 * 4. \"virtual\" tuple consisting of Datum/isnull arrays (TTSOpsVirtual)\n    38\u2192 *\n    39\u2192 *\n    40\u2192 * The first two cases are similar in that they both deal with \"materialized\"\n    41\u2192 * tuples, but resource management is different.  For a tuple in a disk page\n    42\u2192 * we need to hold a pin on the buffer until the TupleTableSlot's reference\n    43\u2192 * to the tuple is dropped; while for a palloc'd tuple we usually want the\n    44\u2192 * tuple pfree'd when the TupleTableSlot's reference is dropped.\n    45\u2192 *\n    46\u2192 * A \"minimal\" tuple is handled similarly to a palloc'd regular tuple.\n    47\u2192 * At present, minimal tuples never are stored in buffers, so there is no\n    48\u2192 * parallel to case 1.  Note that a minimal tuple has no \"system columns\".\n    49\u2192 *\n    50\u2192 * A \"virtual\" tuple is an optimization used to minimize physical data copying\n    51\u2192 * in a nest of plan nodes.  Until materialized pass-by-reference Datums in\n    52\u2192 * the slot point to storage that is not directly associated with the\n    53\u2192 * TupleTableSlot; generally they will point to part of a tuple stored in a\n    54\u2192 * lower plan node's output TupleTableSlot, or to a function result\n    55\u2192 * constructed in a plan node's per-tuple econtext.  It is the responsibility\n    56\u2192 * of the generating plan node to be sure these resources are not released for\n    57\u2192 * as long as the virtual tuple needs to be valid or is materialized.  Note\n    58\u2192 * also that a virtual tuple does not have any \"system columns\".\n    59\u2192 *\n    60\u2192 * The Datum/isnull arrays of a TupleTableSlot serve double duty.  For virtual\n    61\u2192 * slots they are the authoritative data.  For the other builtin slots,\n    62\u2192 * the arrays contain data extracted from the tuple.  (In this state, any\n    63\u2192 * pass-by-reference Datums point into the physical tuple.)  The extracted\n    64\u2192 * information is built \"lazily\", ie, only as needed.  This serves to avoid\n    65\u2192 * repeated extraction of data from the physical tuple.\n    66\u2192 *\n    67\u2192 * A TupleTableSlot can also be \"empty\", indicated by flag TTS_FLAG_EMPTY set\n    68\u2192 * in tts_flags, holding no valid data.  This is the only valid state for a\n    69\u2192 * freshly-created slot that has not yet had a tuple descriptor assigned to\n    70\u2192 * it.  In this state, TTS_FLAG_SHOULDFREE should not be set in tts_flags and\n    71\u2192 * tts_nvalid should be set to zero.\n    72\u2192 *\n    73\u2192 * The tupleDescriptor is simply referenced, not copied, by the TupleTableSlot\n    74\u2192 * code.  The caller of ExecSetSlotDescriptor() is responsible for providing\n    75\u2192 * a descriptor that will live as long as the slot does.  (Typically, both\n    76\u2192 * slots and descriptors are in per-query memory and are freed by memory\n    77\u2192 * context deallocation at query end; so it's not worth providing any extra\n    78\u2192 * mechanism to do more.  However, the slot will increment the tupdesc\n    79\u2192 * reference count if a reference-counted tupdesc is supplied.)\n    80\u2192 *\n    81\u2192 * When TTS_FLAG_SHOULDFREE is set in tts_flags, the physical tuple is \"owned\"\n    82\u2192 * by the slot and should be freed when the slot's reference to the tuple is\n    83\u2192 * dropped.\n    84\u2192 *\n    85\u2192 * tts_values/tts_isnull are allocated either when the slot is created (when\n    86\u2192 * the descriptor is provided), or when a descriptor is assigned to the slot;\n    87\u2192 * they are of length equal to the descriptor's natts.\n    88\u2192 *\n    89\u2192 * The TTS_FLAG_SLOW flag is saved state for\n    90\u2192 * slot_deform_heap_tuple, and should not be touched by any other code.\n    91\u2192 *----------\n    92\u2192 */\n    93\u2192\n    94\u2192/* true = slot is empty */\n    95\u2192#define\t\t\tTTS_FLAG_EMPTY\t\t\t(1 << 1)\n    96\u2192#define TTS_EMPTY(slot)\t(((slot)->tts_flags & TTS_FLAG_EMPTY) != 0)\n    97\u2192\n    98\u2192/* should pfree tuple \"owned\" by the slot? */\n    99\u2192#define\t\t\tTTS_FLAG_SHOULDFREE\t\t(1 << 2)\n   100\u2192#define TTS_SHOULDFREE(slot) (((slot)->tts_flags & TTS_FLAG_SHOULDFREE) != 0)\n   101\u2192\n   102\u2192/* saved state for slot_deform_heap_tuple */\n   103\u2192#define\t\t\tTTS_FLAG_SLOW\t\t(1 << 3)\n   104\u2192#define
